***sonogram.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:sonogram.html>sonogram</a> (67409)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etylcleanup"><span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin" class="extiw" title="w:Latin">Latin</a></span></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="la">sonus</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">sound</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">-gram</i>.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:sonogram.html>sonogram</a></strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">sonograms</b>)
</p>
<ol><li>a medical image produced by ultrasound echo</li>
<li>a spectrogram</li></ol>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:sonogram.html>sonogram</a></strong> (<i>third-person singular simple present</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en 3 | s | pres-form-of" lang="en">sonograms</b>, <i>present participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en pres | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">sonogramming</b>, <i>simple past and past participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en past | and | past | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">sonogrammed</b>)
</p>
<ol><li>To perform a <a href = vnd.unilang:sonogram.html>sonogram</a> upon.</li></ol>
</body>

<p>Compound of <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:soort.html>soort</a></i> + |  <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:genoot.html>genoot</a></i>.

</p>

<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum"><a href = vnd.unilang:sop.html>sop</a></i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Old Dutch">Old Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="odt">*<a href = vnd.unilang:sop.html>sop</a></i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*suppą</i>.

***sopraan.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:sopraan.html>sopraan</a> (23011)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_language" class="extiw" title="w:Italian language">Italian</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="it">soprano</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span>literally <span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">high (voice)</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:sopraan.html>sopraan</a></strong> <span class="gender"><abbr title="feminine gender">f</abbr></span> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl p-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:sopranen.html>sopranen</a></b>, <i>diminutive</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl diminutive-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:sopraan.html>sopraantje</a></b> <span class="gender"><abbr title="neuter gender">n</abbr></span>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">music</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> The soprano, the highest of the four traditional voice <a href = vnd.unilang:registers.html>registers</a>, <a href = vnd.unilang:even.html>even</a> above alto</li>
<li>A soprano or treble, singer or instrument with such natural register</li></ol>

***southside.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:southside.html>southside</a> (53204)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><i class="Latn mention" lang="en">south</i> + |  <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">side</i>
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:southside.html>southside</a></strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">southsides</b>)
</p>
<ol><li>The southern side of a building, street, area etc.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1999</b>,  Brendan <a href = vnd.unilang:o.html>O</a>'Carroll,  <cite>The <a href = vnd.unilang:mammy.html>Mammy</a></cite> | <sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=VqU5HA3h3SICamp;lpg=PT15amp;dq=%22the%20northside%22amp;pg=PT15v=onepageamp;q=%22the%20northside%22amp;f=false">[1]</a></sup>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">The retail section <a href = vnd.unilang:had.html>had</a> two divisions <a href = vnd.unilang:halal.html>-</a> the <b><a href = vnd.unilang:southside.html>southside</a></b> and the northside <a href = vnd.unilang:halal.html>-</a> with Grafton Street being the main shopping street of the <b><a href = vnd.unilang:southside.html>southside</a></b>, and <a href = vnd.unilang:henry.html>Henry</a> Street and Moore Street the flagships of the northside.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2012</b>,  Robert B. Stepto,  <cite>A Home Elsewhere: Reading African American Classics in the Age of Obama</cite> | <sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=KgZ0JBndgF0Camp;lpg=PA53amp;dq=%22southsides%22amp;pg=PA53v=onepageamp;q=%22southsides%22amp;f=false">[2]</a></sup>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">While certain <a href = vnd.unilang:details.html>details</a> indicate that this <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> a black neighborhood up north in a Michigan city, quite possibly <a href = vnd.unilang:detroit.html>Detroit</a> as some have guessed, Morrison <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> deliberately not specific, allowing us to imagine that the "<a href = vnd.unilang:southside.html>Southside</a>" in her story could be any of a number of <b>southsides</b> created by the Negro migrations, including the <b>southsides</b> <a href = vnd.unilang:we.html>we</a> readers may have lived in.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2015</b>,  <a href = vnd.unilang:dale.html>Dale</a> A. Dye,  <cite>Run Between the Raindrops: Author's Preferred Edition</cite> | <sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=F7_YBQAAQBAJamp;lpg=PT98amp;dq=%22the%20southside%22amp;pg=PT98v=onepageamp;q=%22the%20southside%22amp;f=false">[3]</a></sup>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">What <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> apparently most galling to everyone not directly involved in the dirty fight on the <b><a href = vnd.unilang:southside.html>southside</a></b> of the Perfume River <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> that rattyass NVA flag still flying defiantly <a href = vnd.unilang:over.html>over</a> the Citadel on the northside.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li></ol>

***sowieso.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:sowieso.html>sowieso</a> (4513)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>Borrowed from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_language" class="extiw" title="w:German language">German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="de"><a href = vnd.unilang:sowieso.html>sowieso</a></i>. The negated sense <i><a href = vnd.unilang:niet.html>niet</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:sowieso.html>sowieso</a></i> (“not necessarily”) does not exist in German, which uses <i class="Latn mention" lang="de"><a href = vnd.unilang:nicht.html>nicht</a></i> <i class="Latn mention" lang="de">unbedingt</i> instead.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adverb">Adverb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:sowieso.html>sowieso</a></strong>
</p>
<ol><li>anyhow, in any case, anyway
<dl><dd><i><a href = vnd.unilang:het.html>Het</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:maakt.html>maakt</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:me.html>me</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:niet.html>niet</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:uit.html>uit</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:dat.html>dat</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:het.html>het</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:feest.html>feest</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:niet.html>niet</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:doorgaat.html>doorgaat</a>. <a href = vnd.unilang:ik.html>Ik</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:wilde.html>wilde</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:er.html>er</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:sowieso.html>sowieso</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:niet.html>niet</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:naartoe.html>naartoe</a>.</i>
<dl><dd>I don’<a href = vnd.unilang:t.html>t</a> care that the party <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> cancelled. I didn’<a href = vnd.unilang:t.html>t</a> want to go there <b>anyway</b>.</dd></dl></dd></dl></li>
<li>necessarily, in all <a href = vnd.unilang:cases.html>cases</a>
<dl><dd><i><a href = vnd.unilang:duurder.html>Duurder</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:hoeft.html>hoeft</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:niet.html>niet</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:sowieso.html>sowieso</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:beter.html>beter</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:te.html>te</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:zijn.html>zijn</a>.</i>
<dl><dd>More expensive doesn’<a href = vnd.unilang:t.html>t</a> <b>necessarily</b> mean better.</dd></dl></dd></dl></li></ol>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Synonyms">Synonyms</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<ul><li><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content qualifier-content">anyhow</span><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">)</span><span class="ib-colon sense-qualifier-colon">:</span> <span class="Latn" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:toch.html>toch</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:al.html>al</a></span></li>

<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">spake</i>, an Ingvaeonic form of the more usual <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">speke</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Old Dutch">Old Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="odt">*spēka</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*spaikǭ</i>.

***spaniel.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:spaniel.html>spaniel</a> (88013)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>Borrowed from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_French" class="extiw" title="w:Old French">Old French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fro">espaigneul</i> (modern French <i class="Latn mention" lang="fr">épagneul</i>), from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Occitan" class="extiw" title="w:Old Occitan">Old Occitan</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="pro">espaignol</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" class="extiw" title="w:Vulgar Latin">Vulgar Latin</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="la">*Hispāniolus</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">Spanish</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <i class="Latn mention" lang="la">Hispānia</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">Spain</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:spaniel.html>spaniel</a></strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">spaniels</b>)
</p>
<ol><li>Any of various small to medium-sized breeds of gun dog having a broad muzzle, long, wavy fur and long ears that hang at the side of the head, bred for flushing and retrieving game.</li>
<li>A cringing, fawning person.
<ul><li><b>1595</b>: Shakespeare, William, <i>The Two <a href = vnd.unilang:gentlemen.html>Gentlemen</a> of <a href = vnd.unilang:verona.html>Verona</a></i> Act IV, Scene II
<dl><dd><i><a href = vnd.unilang:proteus.html>Proteus</a></i>: Yet, spaniel-like, the more she spurns my love,/The more it grows and fawneth on her still.</dd></dl></li></ul></li></ol>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:spaniel.html>spaniel</a></strong> (<i>third-person singular simple present</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en 3 | s | pres-form-of" lang="en">spaniels</b>, <i>present participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en pres | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">spanielling</b> <i>or</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en pres | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">spanieling</b>, <i>simple past and past participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en past | and | past | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">spanielled</b> <i>or</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en past | and | past | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">spanieled</b>)
</p>
<ol><li>To follow loyally or obsequiously, like a <a href = vnd.unilang:spaniel.html>spaniel</a>.
<ul><li><b>1606</b>: Shakespeare, William, <i>The Tragedy of <a href = vnd.unilang:antony.html>Antony</a> and <a href = vnd.unilang:cleopatra.html>Cleopatra</a></i>
<dl><dd><i><a href = vnd.unilang:antony.html>Antony</a></i>: Do <a href = vnd.unilang:we.html>we</a> shake hands.—All come to this!—The <a href = vnd.unilang:hearts.html>hearts</a> / That <b><a href = vnd.unilang:spaniel.html>spaniel</a>'d</b> <a href = vnd.unilang:me.html>me</a> at <a href = vnd.unilang:heels.html>heels</a>, to whom I <a href = vnd.unilang:gave.html>gave</a> / Their wishes, do discandy, melt their <a href = vnd.unilang:sweets.html>sweets</a></dd></dl></li>
<li>J. Sedgewick (1840)  <cite><a href = vnd.unilang:timon.html>Timon</a>, but not of Athens</cite>, page 200 |  “Always <b>spanielling</b> at the <a href = vnd.unilang:heels.html>heels</a> of power, the mitred Dignitaries displayed, from first to last, the most rancorous hostility against her.”</li>
<li>David S. Bell (2000)  <cite>Presidential Power in Fifth Republic France</cite>, <small>→ISBN</small>, page 30 |  “Hence Duverger's famous question about <a href = vnd.unilang:de.html>de</a> Gaulle's first <b>spanielling</b> Prime Minister <a href = vnd.unilang:makes.html>makes</a> political ('M. Debré, existe-t-il?'), but not constitutional sense.”</li>
<li>Edward James and <a href = vnd.unilang:farah.html>Farah</a> Mendlesohn (2003)  <cite>The Cambridge Companion to Science Fiction</cite>, <small>→ISBN</small>, page 65 | <dl><dd>The genre which differed from the world in order to advocate a better one <a href = vnd.unilang:halal.html>-</a> or the genre which <b>spanielled</b> at <a href = vnd.unilang:heel.html>heel</a> the sensationalist virtual reality world <a href = vnd.unilang:we.html>we</a> will now arguably inhabit till the planet <a href = vnd.unilang:dies.html>dies</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:halal.html>-</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:had.html>had</a> become by 2000, in triumpth or defeat or both, an <i>institution</i> for the <a href = vnd.unilang:telling.html>telling</a> of story.</dd></dl></li></ul></li></ol>
</body>

***spank.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:spank.html>spank</a> (99589)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>Probably imitative.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:spank.html>spank</a></strong> (<i>third-person singular simple present</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en 3 | s | pres-form-of" lang="en">spanks</b>, <i>present participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en pres | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">spanking</b>, <i>simple past and past participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en past | and | past | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">spanked</b>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To beat, smack or <a href = vnd.unilang:slap.html>slap</a> a person's buttocks, with the bare hand or other object, as punishment, gesture, or form of sexual interaction.</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To soundly defeat, to trounce.</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To hit very hard
<ul><li><b>15 September 2018</b>, <a href = vnd.unilang:barney.html>Barney</a> Ronay, <i>The Guardian</i>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.theguardian.com/football/blog/2018/sep/15/finely-tuned-liverpool-are-really-getting-into-jurgen-klopps-groove">Finely tuned Liverpool are really getting into Jürgen Klopp’s groove</a>:
<dl><dd><a href = vnd.unilang:spurs.html>Spurs</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:had.html>had</a> a free-kick on the edge of the Liverpool box. Érik Lamela <b>spanked</b> it low into the wall, got the ball back, played it out to Christian Eriksen.</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">intransitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To move rapidly.
<dl><dd><i>The ship <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> really <b>spanking</b> along.</i></dd></dl></li></ol>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Related_terms">Related <a href = vnd.unilang:terms.html>terms</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<ul><li><span class="Latn" lang="en">spankee</span></li>
<li><span class="Latn" lang="en">spanker</span></li>
<li><span class="Latn" lang="en">unspanked</span></li></ul>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:spank.html>spank</a></strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">spanks</b>)
</p>
<ol><li>An instance of spanking, separately or part of a multiple blows-beating; a smack, <a href = vnd.unilang:swat.html>swat</a>, or <a href = vnd.unilang:slap.html>slap</a>.</li>
<li>A slapping sound, as produced by spanking.</li></ol>
</body>
